<Gmap_id>0x808327c84b9e0ea9:0x405e6b015bbacd7e<//Gmap_id>< Text>
The line was crazy. That alone tells you how good it is.  Ordering was simple, the portions generous and the taste was spot on.

The burrito wasn't packed with 80% rice and beans like many places.  It also wasn't dripping grease.  It was fresh and delicious with the right mix of meat and veggies.  Ate in the car and didn't spill a drop because it was packed so tight.  I will be back!</Text>

<userid>100871290818849472756< /userid>< user_name>

< Review>
I'm a huge churro fan and there are no good or dedicated places for them in SF but there are a few in SJ. Happy to say that this was my first place I tried and I needn't look any further. This place is amazing. The vibe is surprisingly upbeat with loud music but it really grows on you. They serve Mitchell's ice cream for the sundaes, so you know your getting quality. The churros... The churros are spectacular. I went for a round two and got one dipped in chocolate and it was amazing but the quality of the churros make the original, undipped version basically perfection. Still, if you're not a straight up cinnamon sugar addict like me, you'll find an awesome assortment of dips and topping to adorn your churro with. Seriously, this place is legit and we were super surprised. Not because of any lack of presentation -- this place just looks great. It's just we weren't expecting any churro place to be this good.

As a bonus, the owner even gave us free large mango teas. It was slow and we were the only customers in the store. Very nice and refreshing!

This should be your first and final stop if you're looking for your cinnamon sugar fix, churro lovers.<//Review>

< name>
Character by Integrity Act Honest_Irish<//name>

5<//Rating>
<Pics>None< /Pics>< review>
If you don't have the plus membership, GET IT!  Fortunately I upgraded per a mailer promotion they sent me, prior to a cross country road trip I am currently on. I have driven up through Northern California up and beyond north into Florence, Oregon. From there I headed east though Eugene and beyond through Idaho, Utah, Wyoming, Colorado and now currently in Kansas heading south and then east again further. My Infiniti G35 (used) a 2006 has been incredible through dirt roads (Red Feathers Lakes are beautiful in Colorado) and snow, sleet and heavy rain and wind across the country. But I have run out of gas or near enough to not risk engine damage and call for the emergency fuel that comes with the service in Oregon, Idaho, Wyoming and Colorado.

It's not that I have been doing it on purpose but on this trip its what I'm calling an Empathy Tour where if I find areas or people in need I head there and help. And often that has taken me out of the way and off the beaten trail.

Each time that states respective AAA was fast, very polite and friendly and added anywhere from 2 gallon to 5 depending on distance to the next gas station. In Red Feathers Lake Colorado the driver drove 50 miles from Fort Collins up into the hills to get me then asked if I wanted to follow him back down the hill as the snow was really coming down. I could tell he wanted to go faster but kept a slower pace for me. His name was James and I sincerely appreciate his help and compassion. He wants to move to California at which I tried to discourage him. Not because of the AAA offices but in general the businesses are not the best in customer service anymore in comparison to what I've experienced in other states on this trip.

Step it up California vendors to AAA or maybe get into work you actually enjoy.

Over all I highly recommend AAA not just for the basic device but this PLUS is far beyond I expected from the promotion and will gladly re-up on a continuing and mostly lifelong membership save for my time abroad.

The only thing I would suggest to AAA's CEO or President is to calm down with the life insurance mailers. Big expensive envelopes as a promo mailer that I have since 6 times ignored is a waste where that money could go more into infrastructure and salary or benefits raises rather than wasted promo's for more member sales. Other than that, good on ya for leading a great company.</review>

< text>
It's a great taqueria. I always get their chicken burritos when I go there and my wife fell in love with there quesadillas and chicken Nachos. My wife did not like Mexican food before going to this place, she's filipina and an extremely picky eater so that tells you something.They are very generous when they put meat in your choice of order. It's so much it puts other places to shame. I have to add, when I last went there they put lots of onions in my burrito and holy cow!! I tasted even better. There goes my diet....
UPDATE- Our last experience crushed us.... We went to this place the last week of September 2018 and we waited 35 min for our food because they completely forgot about us. I went to the counter and the girl forgot to give the cook our order. When we finally got our food, the cook apologized and I told her it was fine. I loved the food there so it didn't bother me much. Well we took the food home to eat it there and to me and my wifes surprise there was hardly any meat in my chicken burrito and my wifes steak quesadilla barely had any meat inside of it either. She was very upset. I was so happy to finally have a really good taqueria close to home but my last experience left a bad taste in my mouth. The cook they had that day was a older lady. All the other days we went it was a guy cook. They should always have the older guy working there cause the lady cook seems to be very stingy on the amount of meat she puts in the food. I know you may think it's not a big deal but all it takes for us is one bad experience to start thinking twice going back to a place to eat again. They seem like really good people though, but I really don't want to pay $14.00 for a burrito and quesadilla with scraps of meat inside. We walked past their taqueria twice since then to eat at Panda Express or Subways.... I dropped it from 5 stars to 4 stars. I still have high hopes for this place, but if the lady cook sticks around and still makes empty burritos and quesadillas, we will go somewhere else for our mexican food.< /text>

<Text>My legal journey started on 5/15/15, when on a clear day a young lady rear ended me. It was very apparent for at least a quarter mile, that traffic was stopped, but she hit me. She immediately backed up, changed lanes, and took off. I followed her to get her license number if nothing else, but she ultimately pulled over. We exchanged information and I headed home, about 5 miles away. When we stopped, I didn't see much damage to my vehicle and while driving home I thought I wouldn't report it. But by the time I arrived home, both my hands were numb.
Let me back up for a minute... in 1996 I had broken my neck. I had my third spinal surgery in 2000, and the numbness then was gone. From 2000 until 5/15/15, I had no numbness.
With the numbness back, I reported the accident to my insurance. They wanted me to see a doctor because of the previous damage and the return of the numbness. I went that day, x-rays were done. I was sent to physical therapy, and an MRI was performed, which didn't show much, but the numbness continued. Ultimately I had three cervical injections, which relieved the numbness. My choices were more cervical surgery, or periodic injections.
I turned my vehicle, a Honda CRV, into a repair shop for the minor visible damage, and when they took it apart, they found the rear door had been collapsed.
Somewhere in this, I found out the other driver had minimum coverage, that wouldn't be sufficient to cover the damage to my vehicle or to me.
Thats about when I sought legal help. I found Brad Schultz of Demas Law Group. I met with Brad, told him what happened and he took my case.
My case was a bit more complicated due to the injury in 1996, but Brad preserved. He requested my medical records from my doctor of 30+ years, and by the time we were ready for the hearing, Brad knew more of my medical history than I remembered.
Over time, the insurance made a couple settlement offers, but their offers would have left me with thousands of dollars to pay for the medical treatments.
We were ready for the hearing on Friday, but on Thursday the insurance made a reasonable offer to settle, which paid all the medical and I also got a check.
My whole hearted Thank You to Brad Schultz of Demas Law Group, and to his paralegal, Vanessa, who kept me informed along the way.
If you ever find yourself in my situation, I would highly recommend Brad Schultz of Demas Law Group. Brad took the time to fully understand my physical issues, and to pursue a remedy. The insurance wanted to say my problems were from the original injury in 1996, but they weren't.
Brad stood by me the entire time. He spent hours to understand what had happened in my original injury, and the added problems the rear ending created.
I cannot say enough great things about how Brad, Vanessa and Demas Law Group, worked to get a reasonable settlement.</Text>< Pics>

After four surgeries and more than a year of rehab and recovery, I had worked my way to a place where Mr. Demas could begin to assess fair compensation for my injuries. <pics>None< /pics><Date>1443376702447</Date>< Text>
$5 Fridays!

Pavilions, owned by Vons, is a more upscale supermarket.  Fortunately, sale prices are good at both locations.

The layout is easy to decipher and the entirety of the store is kept clean and neat.  A pharmacy, deli, butcher, Starbucks and fresh sushi are on hand to make a one stop shop experience.

What brings me in are $5 Fridays.  From chicken wings to meatloaf, many a deal are to be had for just $5. Another enticement is clearance diving for any good finds I may spot.  Great for finding dinner!

Service has been good.  The deli employees are really great with gathering up what I need.  Parking is in a private lot, shared by Rite Aid and other businesses.

Pavilions is a great place to fulfill your grocery needs.  $5 Fridays are a great way to save & prices are competitive with other markets.

Recommend!<//Text>

< Text>
The employees are friendly here. I am not good about ad shopping or cutting coupons, so I can't honestly say how the prices compare, but I like a clean store that has all of my family's favorites. The convenience of having Rite Aid and Tuesday Morning in the same shopping center makes for one-stop shopping. The reason I don't do 5 stars is not the employees' faults, it's district offices that cut back on staff hours making it difficult to get anyone to help if you have a question or a return. In my days of working the grocery business, there was a customer service counter (that had someone always there) that helped with all of that. Now, you have to stand around waiting a long time for someone to come up and help you or you have to interrupt cashiers who are trying to help get lines down in the checkout lanes. Not good for customer service.<//Text>

<Text>It's funny writing a review for a grocery store... it's so everyday and common that I didn't think it needed a review. But like restaurants and other service industries, the people need to know what to expect when they glide past the sliding doors! Since this is a Pavillions (an extra posh version of a Safeway or Vons), it includes a Starbucks, a full bakery, a full deli, a full butcher, a full florist, and a sushi chef! It's got everything! The cashiers are all really friendly and they always have plenty of courtesy clerks available to help find anything. It's a big store so they have a lot of options on the shelves that the smaller stores don't have. VERY large alcohol selection.< /Text><rate>4</rate>< username>
